<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">The arts</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Creative human and cultural expression</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the group of creative disciplines. For the concept of art, see <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">Art</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Art_(disambiguation)" title="Art (disambiguation)">Art (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Arts" redirects here. For the acronym, see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/ARTS_(disambiguation)" title="ARTS (disambiguation)">ARTS</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

<li><a href="/wiki/Las_Lajas_Shrine" title="Las Lajas Shrine">Las Lajas Shrine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nari%C3%B1o_Department" title="Nariño Department">Nariño Department</a>, Colombia</li>
<li>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bian_Lian" title="Bian Lian">Bian Lian</a> performer.</li></ul></div></div></div></div>
<p><b>The arts</b> are a very wide range of human practices of <a href="/wiki/Creativity" title="Creativity">creative expression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Storytelling" title="Storytelling">storytelling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a> participation. They encompass multiple diverse and plural modes of thinking, doing and being, in an extremely broad range of <a href="/wiki/List_of_art_media" title="List of art media">media</a>. Both highly dynamic and a characteristically constant feature of human life, they have developed into innovative, stylized and sometimes intricate forms. This is often achieved through sustained and deliberate study, training and/or theorizing within a particular tradition, across generations and even between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civilizations" title="Civilizations">civilizations</a>. The arts are a vehicle through which human beings cultivate distinct social, cultural and individual identities, while transmitting values, impressions, judgments, ideas, visions, spiritual meanings, patterns of life and experiences across time and space.
</p><p>Prominent examples of the arts include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Visual_arts" title="Visual arts">visual arts</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceramic_art" title="Ceramic art">ceramics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drawing" title="Drawing">drawing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking" title="Filmmaking">filmmaking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">photography</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculpting</a>),</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literary_arts" title="Literary arts">literary arts</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Fiction" title="Fiction">fiction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drama" title="Drama">drama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prose" title="Prose">prose</a>),</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">theatre</a>) and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Culinary_arts" title="Culinary arts">culinary arts</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Cuisine" title="Cuisine">cooking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chocolatier" title="Chocolatier">chocolate making</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winemaking" title="Winemaking">winemaking</a>).</li></ul>
<p>They can employ <a href="/wiki/Skill" title="Skill">skill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imagination" title="Imagination">imagination</a> to produce <a href="/wiki/Physical_object" title="Physical object">objects</a>, <a href="/wiki/Performance" title="Performance">performances</a>, convey insights and <a href="/wiki/Experience" title="Experience">experiences</a>, and construct new <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environments</a> and spaces.
</p><p>The arts can refer to common, popular or everyday practices as well as more sophisticated and systematic, or institutionalized ones. They can be discrete and self-contained, or combine and interweave with other art forms, such as the combination of artwork with the written word in <a href="/wiki/Comics" title="Comics">comics</a>. They can also develop or contribute to some particular aspect of a more complex art form, as in <a href="/wiki/Cinematography" title="Cinematography">cinematography</a>. By definition, the arts themselves are open to being continually re-defined. The practice of <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a>, for example, is a testament to the shifting boundaries, improvisation and experimentation, reflexive nature, and <a href="/wiki/Self-criticism" title="Self-criticism">self-criticism</a> or questioning that art and its conditions of production, reception, and possibility can undergo.
</p><p>As both a means of developing capacities of attention and sensitivity, and as <a href="/wiki/Art_for_art%27s_sake" title="Art for art's sake">ends in themselves</a>, the arts can simultaneously be a form of response to the world, and a way that our responses, and what we deem worthwhile goals or pursuits, are transformed. From prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Art_of_the_Upper_Paleolithic" title="Art of the Upper Paleolithic">cave paintings</a>, to ancient and contemporary forms of <a href="/wiki/Ritual" title="Ritual">ritual</a>, to modern-day <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">films</a>, art has served to register, embody and preserve our ever shifting relationships to each other and to the world.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Classificatory_disputes_about_art" title="Classificatory disputes about art">Classificatory disputes about art</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts_education" title="Liberal arts education">Liberal arts education</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hans_Rottenhammer_-_Allegory_of_the_Arts_-_WGA20147.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1282" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Hans_Rottenhammer_-_Allegory_of_the_Arts_-_WGA20147.jpg/220px-Hans_Rottenhammer_-_Allegory_of_the_Arts_-_WGA20147.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Hans_Rottenhammer_-_Allegory_of_the_Arts_-_WGA20147.jpg/330px-Hans_Rottenhammer_-_Allegory_of_the_Arts_-_WGA20147.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Hans_Rottenhammer_-_Allegory_of_the_Arts_-_WGA20147.jpg/440px-Hans_Rottenhammer_-_Allegory_of_the_Arts_-_WGA20147.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hans_Rottenhammer_-_Allegory_of_the_Arts_-_WGA20147.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hans_Rottenhammer" title="Hans Rottenhammer">Hans Rottenhammer</a>, <i>Allegory of the Arts</i> (second half of the 16th century). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gem%C3%A4ldegalerie" title="Gemäldegalerie">Gemäldegalerie</a>, Berlin.</div></div></div>
<p>There are several possible meanings for the definitions of the terms <i>Art</i> and <i>Arts</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[a]</a></sup> The first meaning of the word <i>art</i> is " way of doing ".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEValéry1935683_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEValéry1935683-2">[1]</a></sup> The most basic present meaning defines the arts as specific activities that produce sensitivity in humans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-editions-larousse_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-editions-larousse-3">[2]</a></sup> The arts are also referred to as bringing together all creative and imaginative activities, without including science.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[b]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-working-definitions_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-working-definitions-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collins_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-collins-6">[4]</a></sup> In its most basic abstract definition, <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a> is a documented expression of a sentient being through or on an accessible medium so that anyone can view, hear or experience it. The act itself of producing an expression can also be referred to as a certain art, or as art in general. Whether this solidified expression, or the act of producing it, is "good" or has value depends on those who access and rate it. Such public rating is dependent on various subjective factors. <a href="/wiki/Merriam-Webster" title="Merriam-Webster">Merriam-Webster</a> defines "the arts" as "painting, sculpture, music, theatre, literature, etc., considered as a group of activities done by people with skill and imagination."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-merriam-webster_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-merriam-webster-7">[5]</a></sup> Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>, in the National Foundation on the Arts and Humanities Act, defined "the arts" as follows:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The term "the arts" includes, but is not limited to, music (instrumental and vocal), dance, drama, folk art, creative writing, architecture and allied fields, painting, sculpture, photography, graphic and craft arts, industrial design, costume and fashion design, motion pictures, television, radio, film, video, tape and sound recording, the arts related to the presentation, performance, execution, and exhibition of such major art forms, all those traditional arts practiced by the diverse peoples of this country. (<i>sic</i>) and the study and application of the arts to the human environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_Camp2006_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_Camp2006-8">[6]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Art is a global activity in which a large number of disciplines are included, such as: fine arts, liberal arts, visual arts, decorative arts, applied arts, design, crafts, performing arts, and so on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-working-definitions_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-working-definitions-5">[3]</a></sup> We are talking about "the arts" when several of them are mentioned: "As in all arts the enjoyment increases with the knowledge of the art".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHemingway200311_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHemingway200311-9">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>The arts can be divided into several areas, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fine_arts" title="Fine arts">fine arts</a> which bring together, in the broad sense, all the arts whose aim is to produce true aesthetic pleasure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beaux-arts_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-beaux-arts-10">[8]</a></sup> decorative arts and <a href="/wiki/Applied_arts" title="Applied arts">applied arts</a> which relate to an aesthetic side in everyday life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-applied-arts_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-applied-arts-11">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_and_classifications">History and classifications</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_art" title="History of art">History of art</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_music" title="History of music">History of music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_literature" title="History of literature">History of literature</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Venus_of_Brassempouy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="589" data-file-width="741" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Venus_of_Brassempouy.jpg/220px-Venus_of_Brassempouy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Venus_of_Brassempouy.jpg/330px-Venus_of_Brassempouy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Venus_of_Brassempouy.jpg/440px-Venus_of_Brassempouy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Venus_of_Brassempouy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Venus_of_Brassempouy" title="Venus of Brassempouy">Venus of Brassempouy</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, all art and <a href="/wiki/Craft" title="Craft">craft</a> was referred to by the same word, <i><a href="/wiki/Techne" title="Techne">techne</a></i>. Thus, there was no distinction among the arts. <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> art brought the veneration of the animal form and the development of equivalent skills to show musculature, poise, beauty, and anatomically correct proportions. <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Ancient Roman</a> art depicted gods as idealized humans, shown with characteristic distinguishing features (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a>' thunderbolt). In <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_art" title="Byzantine art">Byzantine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_art" title="Gothic art">Gothic art</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the dominance of the church insisted on the expression of biblical truths.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_art" title="Eastern art">Eastern art</a> has generally worked in a style akin to <a href="/wiki/Medieval_art" title="Medieval art">Western medieval art</a>, namely a concentration on surface patterning and local colour (meaning the plain colour of an object, such as basic red for a red robe, rather than the modulations of that colour brought about by light, shade and reflection). A characteristic of this style is that the local colour is often defined by an outline (a contemporary equivalent is the cartoon). This is evident in, for example, the art of <a href="/wiki/Indian_art" title="Indian art">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_art" title="Tibetan art">Tibet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_art" title="Japanese art">Japan</a>. Religious <a href="/wiki/Islamic_art" title="Islamic art">Islamic art</a> forbids iconography, and instead expresses religious ideas through <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">calligraphy</a> and geometrical designs.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classifications">Classifications</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outline_of_the_arts" title="Outline of the arts">Outline of the arts</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catullus-at-Lesbia%27s-large.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1132" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Catullus-at-Lesbia%27s-large.jpg/220px-Catullus-at-Lesbia%27s-large.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Catullus-at-Lesbia%27s-large.jpg/330px-Catullus-at-Lesbia%27s-large.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Catullus-at-Lesbia%27s-large.jpg/440px-Catullus-at-Lesbia%27s-large.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catullus-at-Lesbia%27s-large.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Alma-Tadema" title="Lawrence Alma-Tadema">Lawrence Alma-Tadema</a>'s <i>Catullus-at-Lesbia's</i> (1865)</div></div></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artes_Liberales" title="Artes Liberales">Artes Liberales</a></i> (liberal arts) were taught in European <a href="/wiki/Medieval_university" title="Medieval university">universities</a> as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trivium_(education)" title="Trivium (education)">Trivium</a>, an introductory curriculum involving <a href="/wiki/Grammar" title="Grammar">grammar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhetoric" title="Rhetoric">rhetoric</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Logic#Informal" title="Logic">logic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOnionsFriedrichsenBurchfield1991994_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOnionsFriedrichsenBurchfield1991994-12">[10]</a></sup> and of the <a href="/wiki/Quadrivium" title="Quadrivium">Quadrivium</a>, a curriculum involving the "mathematical arts" of <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic" title="Arithmetic">arithmetic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geometry" title="Geometry">geometry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artes_Mechanicae" title="Artes Mechanicae">Artes Mechanicae</a></i> (consisting of <i>vestiaria</i> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tailoring" title="Tailoring">tailoring</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weaving</a>; <i>agricultura</i> – <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>; <i>architectura</i> – <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Masonry" title="Masonry">masonry</a>; <i>militia</i> and <i>venatoria</i> – <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_education_and_training" title="Military education and training">military education</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts" title="Martial arts">martial arts</a>; <i>mercatura</i> – <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a>; <i>coquinaria</i> – <a href="/wiki/Cooking" title="Cooking">cooking</a>; and <i>metallaria</i> – <a href="/wiki/Blacksmith" title="Blacksmith">blacksmithing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The citation is not specific enough to facilitate source verification (May 2020)">not specific enough to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> were practised and developed in guild environments. The modern distinction between "artistic" and "non-artistic" skills did not develop until the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>. In modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia" title="Academia">academia</a>, the arts are usually grouped with or as a subset of the <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a>. Some subjects in the humanities are <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">history</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguistics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Logic" title="Logic">logic</a>.
</p><p>The arts have also been classified as seven: <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculpture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">performing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">cinema</a>.
Some view literature, painting, sculpture, and music as the main four arts, of which the others are derivative; <a href="/wiki/Drama" title="Drama">drama</a> is literature with <a href="/wiki/Acting" title="Acting">acting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">dance</a> is music expressed through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motion_(physics)" title="Motion (physics)">motion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Song" title="Song">song</a> is music with literature and <a href="/wiki/Human_voice" title="Human voice">voice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERowlandsLandauer2001_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowlandsLandauer2001-15">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">Film</a> is sometimes called the "eighth" and <a href="/wiki/Comics" title="Comics">comics</a> the "ninth art".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual_art" title="Visual art">Visual art</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Plastic_arts" title="Plastic arts">Plastic arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Work_of_art" title="Work of art">Work of art</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">Architecture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ac.parthenon5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="575" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Ac.parthenon5.jpg/220px-Ac.parthenon5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Ac.parthenon5.jpg/330px-Ac.parthenon5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Ac.parthenon5.jpg/440px-Ac.parthenon5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ac.parthenon5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Parthenon" title="Parthenon">Parthenon</a> on top of the <a href="/wiki/Acropolis_of_Athens" title="Acropolis of Athens">Acropolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a></div></div></div>
<p>Architecture is the <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> of <a href="/wiki/Design" title="Design">designing</a> <a href="/wiki/Building" title="Building">buildings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Structure" title="Structure">structures</a>. The word <i>architecture</i> comes from the Greek <i>arkhitekton</i>, "master builder, director of works," from <i>αρχι-</i> (arkhi) "chief" + <i>τεκτων</i> (tekton) "builder, carpenter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarper2016_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarper2016-17">[15]</a></sup> A wider definition would include the design of the built environment, from the macrolevel of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_planning" title="Town planning">town planning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urban_design" title="Urban design">urban design</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Landscape_architecture" title="Landscape architecture">landscape architecture</a> to the microlevel of creating <a href="/wiki/Furniture" title="Furniture">furniture</a>. Architectural design usually must address both feasibility and <a href="/wiki/Cost" title="Cost">cost</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Construction" title="Construction">builder</a>, as well as function and <a href="/wiki/Aesthetics" title="Aesthetics">aesthetics</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Consumer" title="Consumer">user</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Table_of_architecture,_Cyclopaedia,_1728,_volume_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2708" data-file-width="2529" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Table_of_architecture%2C_Cyclopaedia%2C_1728%2C_volume_1.jpg/220px-Table_of_architecture%2C_Cyclopaedia%2C_1728%2C_volume_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Table_of_architecture%2C_Cyclopaedia%2C_1728%2C_volume_1.jpg/330px-Table_of_architecture%2C_Cyclopaedia%2C_1728%2C_volume_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Table_of_architecture%2C_Cyclopaedia%2C_1728%2C_volume_1.jpg/440px-Table_of_architecture%2C_Cyclopaedia%2C_1728%2C_volume_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Table_of_architecture,_Cyclopaedia,_1728,_volume_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Table of architecture, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyclopaedia,_or_an_Universal_Dictionary_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Cyclopaedia, or an Universal Dictionary of Arts and Sciences">Cyclopaedia</a></i>, 1728</div></div></div>
<p>In modern usage, architecture is the <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Discipline" title="Discipline">discipline</a> of creating, or inferring an implied or apparent plan of, a complex object or <a href="/wiki/System" title="System">system</a>. The term can be used to connote the <i>implied architecture</i> of abstract things such as <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, the <i>apparent architecture</i> of natural things, such as <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geological</a> formations or the <a href="/wiki/Structural_biology" title="Structural biology">structure of biological cells</a>, or explicitly <i>planned architectures</i> of human-made things such as <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computers" title="Computers">computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_architecture" title="Enterprise architecture">enterprises</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">databases</a>, in addition to buildings. In every usage, an architecture may be seen as a <i>subjective <a href="/wiki/Map_(mathematics)" title="Map (mathematics)">mapping</a></i> from a human perspective (that of the <i>user</i> in the case of abstract or physical artefacts) to the <a href="/wiki/Element_(mathematics)" title="Element (mathematics)">elements</a> or components of some kind of <a href="/wiki/Structure" title="Structure">structure</a> or system, which preserves the relationships among the elements or components. Planned architecture manipulates space, volume, texture, light, shadow, or abstract elements in order to achieve pleasing <a href="/wiki/Aesthetics" title="Aesthetics">aesthetics</a>. This distinguishes it from <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied science</a> or <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, which usually concentrate more on the functional and feasibility aspects of the design of constructions or structures.
</p><p>In the field of building architecture, the skills demanded of an architect range from the more complex, such as for a <a href="/wiki/Hospital" title="Hospital">hospital</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Stadium" title="Stadium">stadium</a>, to the apparently simpler, such as planning <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Residential" title="Residential">residential</a> houses. Many architectural works may be seen also as cultural and political <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbols</a>, or works of art. The role of the architect, though changing, has been central to the successful (and sometimes less than successful) design and implementation of pleasingly built environments in which people live.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceramics">Ceramics</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ceramic_art" title="Ceramic art">Ceramic art</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MET_DP342705_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2440" data-file-width="2392" decoding="async" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/MET_DP342705_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-MET_DP342705_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/MET_DP342705_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-MET_DP342705_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/MET_DP342705_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-MET_DP342705_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MET_DP342705_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chinese <a href="/wiki/Blue_and_white_pottery" title="Blue and white pottery">blue and white porcelain</a> jar, <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a>, 15th century</div></div></div>
<p>Ceramic art is art made from <a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">ceramic</a> materials (including <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clay</a>), which may take forms such as <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">pottery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tile" title="Tile">tile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Figurine" title="Figurine">figurines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculpture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tableware" title="Tableware">tableware</a>. While some ceramic products are considered <a href="/wiki/Fine_art" title="Fine art">fine art</a>, some are considered to be <a href="/wiki/Decorative_arts" title="Decorative arts">decorative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_design" title="Industrial design">industrial</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Applied_arts" title="Applied arts">applied</a> art objects. Ceramics may also be considered <a href="/wiki/Artifact_(archaeology)" title="Artifact (archaeology)">artefacts</a> in <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeology</a>. Ceramic art can be made by one person or by a group of people. In a pottery or ceramic factory, a group of people design, manufacture, and decorate the pottery. Products from a pottery are sometimes referred to as "art pottery." In a one-person pottery studio, ceramists or potters produce <a href="/wiki/Studio_pottery" title="Studio pottery">studio pottery</a>. In modern ceramic engineering usage, "ceramics" is the art and science of making objects from inorganic, non-metallic materials by the action of heat. It excludes <a href="/wiki/Glass" title="Glass">glass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaic</a> made from glass <i><a href="/wiki/Tessera" title="Tessera">tesserae</a>.</i>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conceptual_art">Conceptual art</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Conceptual_art" title="Conceptual art">Conceptual art</a></div>
<p>Conceptual art is art wherein the concept(s) or idea(s) involved in the work take precedence over traditional aesthetic and material concerns.
The inception of the term in the 1960s referred to a strict and focused practice of idea-based art that often defied traditional visual criteria associated with the visual arts in its presentation as text.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeWitt196779–83_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeWitt196779–83-18">[16]</a></sup> Through its association with the <a href="/wiki/Young_British_Artists" title="Young British Artists">Young British Artists</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Turner_Prize" title="Turner Prize">Turner Prize</a> during the 1990s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntsman2015221_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntsman2015221-19">[17]</a></sup> its popular usage, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, developed as a synonym for all <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a> that does not practise the traditional skills of <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculpture</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drawing">Drawing</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Drawing" title="Drawing">Drawing</a></div>
<p>Drawing is a means of making an <a href="/wiki/Image" title="Image">image</a>, using any of a wide variety of tools and techniques. It generally involves making marks on a surface by applying pressure from a tool, or moving a tool across a surface. Common tools are <a href="/wiki/Graphite" title="Graphite">graphite</a> <a href="/wiki/Pencil" title="Pencil">pencils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pen" title="Pen">pen</a> and ink, <a href="/wiki/Ink" title="Ink">inked</a> <a href="/wiki/Brush" title="Brush">brushes</a>, wax <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colour_pencils" title="Colour pencils">colour pencils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crayon" title="Crayon">crayons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charcoal" title="Charcoal">charcoals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pastel" title="Pastel">pastels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marker_pen" title="Marker pen">markers</a>. Digital tools which can simulate the effects of these are also used. The main techniques used in drawing are line drawing, <a href="/wiki/Hatching" title="Hatching">hatching</a>, crosshatching, random hatching, scribbling, <a href="/wiki/Stippling" title="Stippling">stippling</a>, and blending. An <a href="/wiki/Artist" title="Artist">artist</a> who excels in drawing is referred to as a <i>drafter</i>, <i>draftswoman</i>, or <i>draughtsman</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> Drawing can be used to create art used in cultural industries such as <a href="/wiki/Illustration" title="Illustration">illustrations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comics" title="Comics">comics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animation</a>. Comics are often called the "ninth art" (le neuvième art) in Francophone scholarship, adding to the traditional "Seven Arts".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200723_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200723-21">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Painting">Painting</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">Painting</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mona_Lisa,_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci,_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="11146" data-file-width="7479" decoding="async" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg/170px-Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg/255px-Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg/340px-Mona_Lisa%2C_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci%2C_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mona_Lisa,_by_Leonardo_da_Vinci,_from_C2RMF_retouched.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i><a href="/wiki/Mona_Lisa" title="Mona Lisa">Mona Lisa</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a></div></div></div>
<p>Painting is a mode of creative expression, and can be done in numerous forms. <a href="/wiki/Drawing" title="Drawing">Drawing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gesture" title="Gesture">gesture</a> (as in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gestural_painting" title="Gestural painting">gestural painting</a>), <a href="/wiki/Composition_(visual_arts)" title="Composition (visual arts)">composition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narrative" title="Narrative">narration</a> (as in <a href="/wiki/Narrative_art" title="Narrative art">narrative art</a>), or <a href="/wiki/Abstraction" title="Abstraction">abstraction</a> (as in <a href="/wiki/Abstract_art" title="Abstract art">abstract art</a>), among other aesthetic modes, may serve to manifest the expressive and conceptual intention of the practitioner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerry201485_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerry201485-22">[20]</a></sup> Paintings can be naturalistic and representational (as in a <a href="/wiki/Still_life" title="Still life">still life</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landscape_art" title="Landscape art">landscape painting</a>), <a href="/wiki/Photorealism" title="Photorealism">photographic</a>, abstract, narrative, <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbolistic</a> (as in <a href="/wiki/Symbolism_(arts)" title="Symbolism (arts)">Symbolist art</a>), <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">emotive</a> (as in <a href="/wiki/Expressionism" title="Expressionism">Expressionism</a>), or <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">political</a> in nature (as in <a href="/wiki/Artivism" title="Artivism">Artivism</a>).
</p><p>Modern painters have extended the practice considerably to include, for example, <a href="/wiki/Collage" title="Collage">collage</a>. Collage is not painting in the strict sense since it includes other materials. Some modern painters incorporate different materials such as <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Straw" title="Straw">straw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wood" title="Wood">wood</a> or strands of hair for their <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Texture_(painting)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Texture (painting) (page does not exist)">artwork texture</a>. Examples of this are the works of <a href="/wiki/Jean_Dubuffet" title="Jean Dubuffet">Jean Dubuffet</a> or <a href="/wiki/Anselm_Kiefer" title="Anselm Kiefer">Anselm Kiefer</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Photography">Photography</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fine_art_photography" title="Fine art photography">Fine art photography</a></div>
<p>Photography as an art form refers to photographs that are created in accordance with the creative vision of the photographer. Art photography stands in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Photojournalism" title="Photojournalism">photojournalism</a>, which provides a visual account for news events, and commercial photography, the primary focus of which is to advertise products or services.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sculpture">Sculpture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">Sculpture</a></div>
<p>Sculpture is the branch of the <a href="/wiki/Visual_arts" title="Visual arts">visual arts</a> that operates in three dimensions. It is one of the <a href="/wiki/Plastic_arts" title="Plastic arts">plastic arts</a>. Durable sculptural processes originally used <a href="/wiki/Carving" title="Carving">carving</a> (the removal of material) and modelling (the addition of material, as clay), in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stone" title="Stone">stone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metal" title="Metal">metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceramic_art" title="Ceramic art">ceramics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wood" title="Wood">wood</a> and other materials; but since <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernism</a>, shifts in sculptural process led to an almost complete freedom of materials and process. A wide variety of materials may be worked by removal such as carving, assembled by <a href="/wiki/Welding" title="Welding">welding</a> or modelling, or <a href="/wiki/Molding_(process)" title="Molding (process)">moulded</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Casting" title="Casting">cast</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literary_arts">Literary arts</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">Language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">Literature</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097025294">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096940132">.mw-parser-output .listen .side-box-text{line-height:1.1em}.mw-parser-output .listen-plain{border:none;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded{width:100%;margin:0;border-width:1px 0 0 0;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-header{padding:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded .listen-header{padding:2px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen-file-header{padding:4px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen .description{padding-top:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen .mw-tmh-player{max-width:100%}@media(max-width:719px){.mw-parser-output .listen{clear:both}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .listen:not(.listen-noimage){width:320px}.mw-parser-output .listen-left{overflow:visible;float:left}.mw-parser-output .listen-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint">
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:Sonnet18.ogg" title="File:Sonnet18.ogg">Sonnet 18</a></div>
<div><audio controls="" data-durationhint="52" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Sonnet18.ogg" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:232px;" width="232"><source data-bandwidth="71535" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (72 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/Sonnet18.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="105584" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/ad/Sonnet18.ogg/Sonnet18.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio></div>
<div class="description"><i><b><a href="/wiki/Sonnet_18" title="Sonnet 18">Sonnet 18</a></b></i> by <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a> part of the Fair Youth <a href="/wiki/Sonnet_sequence" title="Sonnet sequence">sequence</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sonnet" title="Sonnet">sonnets</a>.</div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr/><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<p>Literature is literally "acquaintance with letters" as in the first sense given in the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i>. The noun "literature" comes from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word <i>littera</i> meaning "an individual written character (<a href="/wiki/Letter_(alphabet)" title="Letter (alphabet)">letter</a>)." The term has generally come to identify a collection of <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">writings</a>, which in <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a> are mainly <a href="/wiki/Prose" title="Prose">prose</a> (both <a href="/wiki/Fiction" title="Fiction">fiction</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-fiction" title="Non-fiction">non-fiction</a>), <a href="/wiki/Drama" title="Drama">drama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a>. In much, if not all of the world, the artistic linguistic expression can be <a href="/wiki/Oral_literature" title="Oral literature">oral</a> as well, and include such <a href="/wiki/Genre" title="Genre">genres</a> as <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">epic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legend" title="Legend">legend</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mythology" title="Mythology">myth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ballad" title="Ballad">ballad</a>, other forms of oral <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a>, and as <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folktale</a>. <a href="/wiki/Comics" title="Comics">Comics</a>, the combination of drawings or other visual arts with narrating literature, are often called the "ninth art" (le neuvième art) in Francophone scholarship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller200723_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller200723-21">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">Performing arts</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maasai-Adumu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1283" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Maasai-Adumu.jpg/310px-Maasai-Adumu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Maasai-Adumu.jpg/465px-Maasai-Adumu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Maasai-Adumu.jpg/620px-Maasai-Adumu.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maasai-Adumu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Adumu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Adumu (page does not exist)">Adumu</a>, a traditional <a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai</a> jumping dance</div></div></div>
<p>Performing arts comprise <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mime" title="Mime">mime</a>, and other art forms in which a human performance is the principal product. Performing arts are distinguished by this performance element in contrast with disciplines such as visual and literary arts where the product is an object that does not require a performance to be observed and experienced. Each discipline in the performing arts is temporal in nature, meaning the product is performed over a period of time. Products are broadly categorized as being either repeatable (for example, by script or score) or improvised for each performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHonderich2006_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHonderich2006-23">[21]</a></sup> Artists who participate in these arts in front of an audience are called <i>performers</i>, including <a href="/wiki/Actor" title="Actor">actors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magic_(illusion)" title="Magic (illusion)">magicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comedian" title="Comedian">comedians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dancer" title="Dancer">dancers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musician" title="Musician">musicians</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Singer" title="Singer">singers</a>. Performing arts are also supported by the services of other artists or essential workers, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Songwriting" title="Songwriting">songwriting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stagecraft" title="Stagecraft">stagecraft</a>. Performers often adapt their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physical_appearance" title="Physical appearance">appearance</a> with tools such as <a href="/wiki/Costume" title="Costume">costume</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theatrical_makeup" title="Theatrical makeup">stage makeup</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dance">Dance</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">Dance</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">Dance</a> generally refers to human <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motion_(physics)" title="Motion (physics)">movement</a> either used as a form of expression or presented in a <a href="/wiki/Social" title="Social">social</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spiritual</a> or <a href="/wiki/Performance" title="Performance">performance</a> setting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraleigh19873_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraleigh19873-24">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE''OED''§&amp;nbsp;1_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE''OED''§&amp;nbsp;1-25">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[c]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Choreography_(dance)" title="Choreography (dance)">Choreography</a> is the art of making dances,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinHalfyard2011§_para._1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinHalfyard2011§_para._1-31">[28]</a></sup> and the person who does this is called a choreographer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinHalfyard2011§_para._3_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinHalfyard2011§_para._3-32">[29]</a></sup> Definitions of what constitutes dance are dependent on <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">social</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aesthetic" title="Aesthetic">aesthetic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artistic" title="Artistic">artistic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moral" title="Moral">moral</a> constraints and range from functional movement (such as <a href="/wiki/Folk_dance" title="Folk dance">Folk dance</a>) to codified, <a href="/wiki/Virtuoso" title="Virtuoso">virtuoso</a> techniques such as <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnastics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">figure skating</a> and <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_swimming" title="Synchronized swimming">synchronized swimming</a> are dance disciplines while <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts" title="Martial arts">Martial arts</a> "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kata_(martial_arts)" title="Kata (martial arts)">kata</a>" are often compared to dances.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">Music</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MozartExcerptK331.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="313" data-file-width="625" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/MozartExcerptK331.svg/220px-MozartExcerptK331.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/MozartExcerptK331.svg/330px-MozartExcerptK331.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/MozartExcerptK331.svg/440px-MozartExcerptK331.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MozartExcerptK331.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Sheet_music" title="Sheet music">musical score</a> of the opening <a href="/wiki/Bar_(music)" title="Bar (music)">measures</a> from <a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._11_(Mozart)" title="Piano Sonata No. 11 (Mozart)">Piano Sonata No. 11</a> by <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>. <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:MozartExcerptK331.mid" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/MozartExcerptK331.mid" title="MozartExcerptK331.mid">Play</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:MozartExcerptK331.mid" title="File:MozartExcerptK331.mid"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span></div></div></div>
<p>Music is often defined as an art form whose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_(arts)" title="Media (arts)">medium</a> is the combination of <a href="/wiki/Sound" title="Sound">sounds</a>.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTENettl2001§I_"3._General_encyclopedias":_"There_may_be_disagreement_on_the_need_for_explicit_definition,_but_all_these_works_maintain_that_music_involves_sounds_and_their_combination,_that_it_is_both_art_and_science"_33-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTENettl2001§I_"3._General_encyclopedias":_"There_may_be_disagreement_on_the_need_for_explicit_definition,_but_all_these_works_maintain_that_music_involves_sounds_and_their_combination,_that_it_is_both_art_and_science"-33'>[30]</a></sup> Though scholars agree that music generally consists of <a href="/wiki/Elements_of_music" title="Elements of music">a few core elements</a>, their exact definitions are debated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGardner1983104_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGardner1983104-34">[31]</a></sup> Commonly identified aspects include <a href="/wiki/Pitch_(music)" title="Pitch (music)">pitch</a> (which governs melody and harmony), <a href="/wiki/Duration_(music)" title="Duration (music)">duration</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">rhythm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a>), intensity (including dynamics) and <a href="/wiki/Timbre" title="Timbre">timbre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOwen20006_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOwen20006-35">[32]</a></sup> Though considered a <a href="/wiki/Cultural_universal" title="Cultural universal">cultural universal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Definition_of_music" title="Definition of music">definitions of music</a> vary wildly throughout the world as they are based on diverse views of <a href="/wiki/Nature" title="Nature">nature</a>, the supernatural, and humanity.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTENettl2001§I_"5._Looking_to_the_vernacular_and_to_behaviour"_36-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTENettl2001§I_"5._Looking_to_the_vernacular_and_to_behaviour"-36'>[33]</a></sup> Music is often differentiated into <a href="/wiki/Musical_composition" title="Musical composition">composition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Performance" title="Performance">performance</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Musical_improvisation" title="Musical improvisation">musical improvisation</a> may be regarded as an intermediary tradition.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTENettl2001§III_"5._Music_among_the_arts"_37-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTENettl2001§III_"5._Music_among_the_arts"-37'>[34]</a></sup> Music can be divided into genres and subgenres, although the dividing lines and relationships between music genres are often subtle, sometimes open to individual interpretation, and occasionally controversial.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTENettl2001§III_"6._Classification_or_Typology"_38-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTENettl2001§III_"6._Classification_or_Typology"-38'>[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">Theatre</a></div>
<p>Theatre or theater (from Greek <i>theatron</i> (<i>θέατρον)</i>; from <i>theasthai</i>, "behold"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup>) is the branch of the <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a> concerned with <a href="/wiki/Acting" title="Acting">acting</a> out stories in front of an audience using combinations of speech, gesture, music, dance, sound and spectacle – indeed, any one or more elements of the other performing arts. In addition to the standard narrative dialogue style, theatre takes such forms as <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mime_artist" title="Mime artist">mime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kabuki" title="Kabuki">kabuki</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Indian_dance" title="Classical Indian dance">classical Indian dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_opera" title="Chinese opera">Chinese opera</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mummers_Play" title="Mummers Play">mummers' plays</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Multidisciplinary_artistic_works">Multidisciplinary artistic works</span></h2>
<p>Areas exist in which artistic works incorporate multiple artistic fields, such as <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">film</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Performance_art" title="Performance art">performance art</a>. While opera is often categorized in the performing arts of music, the word itself is Italian for "works", because opera combines several artistic disciplines in a singular artistic experience. In a typical traditional <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, the entire work utilizes the following: the sets (visual arts), costumes (fashion), acting (dramatic performing arts), the libretto, or the words/story (literature), and singers and an orchestra (music).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ernestine_Schumann-Heink_as_Waltraute.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Ernestine_Schumann-Heink_as_Waltraute.png/220px-Ernestine_Schumann-Heink_as_Waltraute.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Ernestine_Schumann-Heink_as_Waltraute.png/330px-Ernestine_Schumann-Heink_as_Waltraute.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Ernestine_Schumann-Heink_as_Waltraute.png/440px-Ernestine_Schumann-Heink_as_Waltraute.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ernestine_Schumann-Heink_as_Waltraute.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ernestine_Schumann-Heink" title="Ernestine Schumann-Heink">Ernestine Schumann-Heink</a> as Waltraute</div></div></div>
<p>The composer <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a> recognized the fusion of so many disciplines into a single work of opera, exemplified by his cycle <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Ring_des_Nibelungen" title="Der Ring des Nibelungen">Der Ring des Nibelungen</a></i> ("The Ring of the Nibelung"). He did not use the term opera for his works, but instead <a href="/wiki/Gesamtkunstwerk" title="Gesamtkunstwerk">Gesamtkunstwerk</a> ("synthesis of the arts"), sometimes referred to as "Music Drama" in English, emphasizing the literary and theatrical components which were as important as the music. Classical <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a> is another form which emerged in the 17th century in which orchestral music is combined with dance.
</p><p>Other works in the late 19th, 20th and 21st centuries have fused other disciplines in unique and creative ways, such as <a href="/wiki/Performance_art" title="Performance art">performance art</a>. Performance art is a performance over time which combines any number of instruments, objects, and art within a predefined or less well-defined structure, some of which can be improvised. Performance art may be scripted, unscripted, random or carefully organized; even audience participation may occur. <a href="/wiki/John_Cage" title="John Cage">John Cage</a> is regarded by many as a performance artist rather than a composer, although he preferred the latter term. He did not compose for traditional ensembles. Cage's composition <i><a href="/wiki/Living_Room_Music" title="Living Room Music">Living Room Music</a></i> composed in 1940 is a "quartet" for unspecified instruments, really non-melodic objects, which can be found in a living room of a typical house, hence the title.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_arts">Other arts</span></h2>
<p>There is no clear line between art and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>. Cultural fields like <a href="/wiki/Gastronomy" title="Gastronomy">gastronomy</a> are sometimes considered as arts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDesaiDeSimoneHenig2013_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDesaiDeSimoneHenig2013-40">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Applied_arts">Applied arts</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Applied_arts" title="Applied arts">Applied arts</a></div>
<p>The applied arts are the application of design and decoration to everyday, functional, objects to make them aesthetically pleasing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChilvers200429_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChilvers200429-41">[38]</a></sup> The applied arts includes fields such as industrial design, illustration, and commercial art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dictionary.com_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-dictionary.com-42">[39]</a></sup> The term "applied art" is used in distinction to the fine arts, where the latter is defined as arts that aims to produce objects which are beautiful or provide intellectual stimulation but have no primary everyday function. In practice, the two often overlap.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Video_games_as_an_art_form" title="Video games as an art form">Video games as an art form</a></div>
<p>A debate exists in the fine arts and <a href="/wiki/Video_game_culture" title="Video game culture">video game cultures</a> over whether video games can be counted as an art form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParker201242_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParker201242-43">[40]</a></sup> Game designer <a href="/wiki/Hideo_Kojima" title="Hideo Kojima">Hideo Kojima</a> professes that video games are a type of service, not an art form, because they are meant to entertain and attempt to entertain as many people as possible, rather than being a single artistic voice (despite Kojima himself being considered a gaming auteur, and the mixed opinions his games typically receive). However, he acknowledged that since video games are made up of artistic elements (for example, the visuals), game designers could be considered museum curators – not creating artistic pieces but arranging them in a way that displays their artistry and sells tickets.
</p><p>Within social sciences, cultural economists show how video games playing is conducive to the involvement in more traditional art forms and cultural practices, which suggests the complementarity between video games and the arts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBorowieckiPrieto-Rodriguez2013239–258_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBorowieckiPrieto-Rodriguez2013239–258-44">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2011, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Endowment_of_the_Arts" title="National Endowment of the Arts">National Endowment of the Arts</a> included video games in its redefinition of what is considered a "work of art" when applying for a grant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarber2012_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarber2012-45">[42]</a></sup> In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_American_Art_Museum" title="Smithsonian American Art Museum">Smithsonian American Art Museum</a> presented an exhibit, <i>The Art of the Video Game</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParker201246_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParker201246-46">[43]</a></sup> Reviews of the exhibit were mixed, including questioning whether video games belong in an art museum.
</p>

</li>
